{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_016sMh52voucJHGwcMGoHsDF","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01WAM8n3mXhMErKh87eXuQm5","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/logs/agent/solution.md","content":"# Kafka Producer Buffer Pool Race Condition - Analysis and Fix\n\n## Files Examined\n\n- **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java** — Entry point for bug investigation; contains `sendProducerData()` and `failBatch()` methods\n- **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/ProducerBatch.java** — Batch lifecycle management; contains `records()` and `completeExceptionally()` methods\n- **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/RecordAccumulator.java** — Buffer pool management; contains `deallocate()` method\n- **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/BufferPool.java** — Buffer memory pooling (referenced via RecordAccumulator)\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n1. **Symptom observed in**: Produce requests silently corrupt topic/partition information; messages appear on wrong topic\n2. **Called from**: `Sender.sendProducerData()` (line 357) — orchestrates batch draining, expiration, and sending\n3. **Batch lifecycle**:\n   - Line 395: Batches drained from accumulator\n   - Line 396: Batches added to `inFlightBatches` tracking map\n   - Line 406-408: Expired batches detected from `inFlightBatches`\n   - Line 418: `failBatch()` called on expired batches\n   - Line 442: `sendProduceRequests()` sends non-expired batches to network client\n4. **Buffer deallocation path**:\n   - Line 835: `failBatch()` calls `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` (line 173)\n   - Line 173: Calls `accumulator.deallocate(batch)`\n   - RecordAccumulator line 1032: Buffer returned to pool via `free.deallocate(batch.buffer())`\n5. **Network client serialization**:\n   - Line 914: `client.send(clientRequest)` queues request for serialization\n   - Serialization happens later during `client.poll()` (line 340)\n   - Serialization reads from `batch.records()` buffer (line 874)\n\n## Root Cause\n\n- **File**: `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java`\n- **Function**: `failBatch()` (line 817-837) and call chain from `sendProducerData()` (line 357)\n- **Line**: ~418 (expiration handling) and ~835 (deallocation)\n- **Exact issue**: Line 835 calls `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch)` unconditionally after marking batch as failed\n\n## Explanation of the Race Condition\n\n### The Bug\n\nWhen a `ProducerBatch` expires while its network request is still queued in the network client's send buffer, the following race occurs:\n\n1. **Iteration N of `sendProducerData()`**:\n   - Line 395: Batch A is drained and added to local `batches` map\n   - Line 396: Batch A is added to `inFlightBatches` (tracking map)\n   - Line 914: `client.send()` queues Batch A's produce request for later serialization\n\n2. **Before network client serialization** (within same or next iteration):\n   - Line 406-408: Batch A is found in `expiredInflightBatches` (delivery timeout reached)\n   - Line 418: `failBatch(Batch A)` is called\n   - Line 825: `batch.completeExceptionally()` returns true (first time setting final state to FAILED)\n   - Line 835: `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(Batch A)` is called\n   - Line 173: `accumulator.deallocate(Batch A)` is called\n   - RecordAccumulator line 1032: Batch A's ByteBuffer is returned to the `BufferPool`\n\n3. **BufferPool reuse** (concurrent with network serialization):\n   - BufferPool allocates Batch A's buffer to Batch B (new batch)\n   - Batch B writes records to the buffer\n\n4. **Network client serialization**:\n   - `client.poll()` (line 340) processes the queued request for Batch A\n   - Request serialization calls `batch.records()` (ProducerBatch line 481)\n   - `recordsBuilder.build()` returns MemoryRecords wrapping the original buffer\n   - **MemoryRecords does NOT copy data; it merely wraps the ByteBuffer reference**\n   - Serialization reads from the buffer, which now contains Batch B's data\n   - **Result**: Produce request header contains Batch B's topic/partition information instead of Batch A's\n\n### Why This Corrupts the Topic Name\n\nThe produce request format has two parts:\n1. **Header** (contains topic name, partition, etc.) — part of ProduceRequest structure\n2. **Records payload** — MemoryRecords wrapping the batch's ByteBuffer\n\nThe header is serialized from the batch's metadata AFTER the buffer has been deallocated and reused. When the buffer is reused, the topic name in the header becomes corrupted with data from the reused buffer.\n\n### Why CRC Validation Passes\n\nThe CRC checksum (ProduceResponse) covers only:\n- Key/value data\n- Headers\n- **NOT** the topic name (which is in the request header, not the record batch)\n\nTherefore, corrupted topic names bypass CRC validation.\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\nThe root cause is that `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` is called in `failBatch()` while the batch's request may still be queued in the network client.\n\n### Fix Strategy\n\n**Do NOT deallocate batches in the `failBatch()` path. Let them be deallocated through the normal response path in `handleProduceResponse()` or through explicit cleanup on disconnect.**\n\n### Code Changes\n\n**File**: `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java`\n\n#### Change 1: Remove premature deallocation in failBatch()\n\n```diff\n--- a/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java\n+++ b/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java\n@@ -828,13 +828,22 @@ public class Sender implements Runnable {\n      * we need to reset the producer id here.\n      */\n     private void failBatch(\n         ProducerBatch batch,\n         RuntimeException topLevelException,\n         Function<Integer, RuntimeException> recordExceptions,\n         boolean adjustSequenceNumbers\n     ) {\n         this.sensors.recordErrors(batch.topicPartition.topic(), batch.recordCount);\n\n         if (batch.completeExceptionally(topLevelException, recordExceptions)) {\n             if (transactionManager != null) {\n                 try {\n                     // This call can throw an exception in the rare case that there's an invalid state transition\n                     // attempted. Catch these so as not to interfere with the rest of the logic.\n                     transactionManager.handleFailedBatch(batch, topLevelException, adjustSequenceNumbers);\n                 } catch (Exception e) {\n                     log.debug(\\\"Encountered error when transaction manager was handling a failed batch\\\", e);\n                 }\n             }\n-            maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);\n+            // Note: We do NOT deallocate the batch here, even though its final state is now set to FAILED.\n+            // The batch may still have an active request queued in the network client's send buffer.\n+            // Deallocating the buffer here would cause the buffer to be returned to the pool and potentially\n+            // reused by another batch while the network client is still serializing this batch's request.\n+            // This would corrupt the serialized request data (topic name, partition, etc).\n+            // Instead, we only remove the batch from inFlightBatches tracking. The buffer will be deallocated\n+            // when the response is eventually received (or the connection times out/disconnects) in handleProduceResponse().\n+            maybeRemoveFromInflightBatches(batch);\n         }\n     }\n```\n\n#### Change 2: Handle deallocation of failed batches that complete through handleProduceResponse()\n\nThe existing code in `handleProduceResponse()` already handles deallocation properly:\n- Line 750 in `completeBatch()`: `if (batch.complete(...)) { maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch); }`\n\nThis code attempts to set the batch's final state to SUCCEEDED. If the batch was already marked FAILED, this will fail gracefully (ProducerBatch.done line 277-286 handles the FAILED -> SUCCEEDED transition by logging and ignoring). The batch will remain in `inFlightBatches` until:\n\n1. A response from broker arrives and is processed in `handleProduceResponse()`\n2. Network disconnect is detected (handled in same method at line 577-582)\n3. Request timeout occurs (handled at line 571-576)\n\nIn all these cases, `completeBatch()` is called which will deallocate the batch at line 750 via `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()`.\n\n#### Change 3: Add defensive guard for batches already deallocated\n\nTo handle any edge cases where a batch might be processed twice, add safety check in `deallocate()`:\n\n```diff\n--- a/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/RecordAccumulator.java\n+++ b/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/RecordAccumulator.java\n@@ -1027,8 +1027,14 @@ public class RecordAccumulator {\n      */\n     public void deallocate(ProducerBatch batch) {\n         incomplete.remove(batch);\n         // Only deallocate the batch if it is not a split batch because split batch are allocated outside the\n         // buffer pool.\n         if (!batch.isSplitBatch())\n-            free.deallocate(batch.buffer(), batch.initialCapacity());\n+            // Only deallocate if the batch still has its buffer. In rare cases, the batch might be\n+            // processed multiple times (e.g., marked failed via timeout, then receives response from broker).\n+            // Once deallocated, the buffer reference becomes invalid.\n+            if (batch.buffer() != null) {\n+                free.deallocate(batch.buffer(), batch.initialCapacity());\n+            }\n     }\n```\n\n## Analysis: Execution Flow Demonstrating the Bug\n\n### Normal (non-buggy) case:\n1. Batch drained at T1, request queued at T2, serialized at T3, response received at T4, deallocated at T4\n2. Buffer stays allocated while network client owns the request\n\n### Buggy case (what we fixed):\n1. Batch drained at T1\n2. Request queued at T2\n3. **Batch expires and marked FAILED at T2.5**\n4. **Buffer deallocated and returned to pool at T2.7**\n5. **New batch B allocated and reuses buffer at T2.8**\n6. Network client serializes request for batch A at T3\n7. **Corruption: Request has batch B's data in the buffer**\n8. Corrupted request sent to broker at T4\n9. Messages appear on wrong topic\n\n### Fixed case:\n1. Batch drained at T1\n2. Request queued at T2\n3. Batch expires and marked FAILED at T2.5\n4. **Buffer NOT deallocated** (fix prevents this)\n5. Network client serializes request for batch A at T3\n6. **Request has correct data from batch A's buffer**\n7. Response received at T4\n8. Batch deallocated at T4 (in handleProduceResponse)\n9. Buffer can now be reused safely\n\n## Summary\n\nThe race condition occurs because `failBatch()` deallocates a batch's buffer before the network client finishes serializing its request. By moving the deallocation to the `handleProduceResponse()` path (which is guaranteed to execute after serialization), we ensure the buffer remains valid throughout the entire request lifecycle.\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":8,"cache_creation_input_tokens":6074,"cache_read_input_tokens":75658,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":6074},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"c1b923c8-4921-46ac-a8e2-6b56aeb6b3d2","uuid":"7e5ae08c-46d4-44c2-b75c-d15840196f94"}
{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01WAM8n3mXhMErKh87eXuQm5","type":"tool_result","content":"File created successfully at: /logs/agent/solution.md"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"c1b923c8-4921-46ac-a8e2-6b56aeb6b3d2","uuid":"ca1d7440-5b3d-4068-9076-0f6efd9d616d","tool_use_result":{"type":"create","filePath":"/logs/agent/solution.md","content":"# Kafka Producer Buffer Pool Race Condition - Analysis and Fix\n\n## Files Examined\n\n- **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java** — Entry point for bug investigation; contains `sendProducerData()` and `failBatch()` methods\n- **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/ProducerBatch.java** — Batch lifecycle management; contains `records()` and `completeExceptionally()` methods\n- **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/RecordAccumulator.java** — Buffer pool management; contains `deallocate()` method\n- **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/BufferPool.java** — Buffer memory pooling (referenced via RecordAccumulator)\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n1. **Symptom observed in**: Produce requests silently corrupt topic/partition information; messages appear on wrong topic\n2. **Called from**: `Sender.sendProducerData()` (line 357) — orchestrates batch draining, expiration, and sending\n3. **Batch lifecycle**:\n   - Line 395: Batches drained from accumulator\n   - Line 396: Batches added to `inFlightBatches` tracking map\n   - Line 406-408: Expired batches detected from `inFlightBatches`\n   - Line 418: `failBatch()` called on expired batches\n   - Line 442: `sendProduceRequests()` sends non-expired batches to network client\n4. **Buffer deallocation path**:\n   - Line 835: `failBatch()` calls `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` (line 173)\n   - Line 173: Calls `accumulator.deallocate(batch)`\n   - RecordAccumulator line 1032: Buffer returned to pool via `free.deallocate(batch.buffer())`\n5. **Network client serialization**:\n   - Line 914: `client.send(clientRequest)` queues request for serialization\n   - Serialization happens later during `client.poll()` (line 340)\n   - Serialization reads from `batch.records()` buffer (line 874)\n\n## Root Cause\n\n- **File**: `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java`\n- **Function**: `failBatch()` (line 817-837) and call chain from `sendProducerData()` (line 357)\n- **Line**: ~418 (expiration handling) and ~835 (deallocation)\n- **Exact issue**: Line 835 calls `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch)` unconditionally after marking batch as failed\n\n## Explanation of the Race Condition\n\n### The Bug\n\nWhen a `ProducerBatch` expires while its network request is still queued in the network client's send buffer, the following race occurs:\n\n1. **Iteration N of `sendProducerData()`**:\n   - Line 395: Batch A is drained and added to local `batches` map\n   - Line 396: Batch A is added to `inFlightBatches` (tracking map)\n   - Line 914: `client.send()` queues Batch A's produce request for later serialization\n\n2. **Before network client serialization** (within same or next iteration):\n   - Line 406-408: Batch A is found in `expiredInflightBatches` (delivery timeout reached)\n   - Line 418: `failBatch(Batch A)` is called\n   - Line 825: `batch.completeExceptionally()` returns true (first time setting final state to FAILED)\n   - Line 835: `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(Batch A)` is called\n   - Line 173: `accumulator.deallocate(Batch A)` is called\n   - RecordAccumulator line 1032: Batch A's ByteBuffer is returned to the `BufferPool`\n\n3. **BufferPool reuse** (concurrent with network serialization):\n   - BufferPool allocates Batch A's buffer to Batch B (new batch)\n   - Batch B writes records to the buffer\n\n4. **Network client serialization**:\n   - `client.poll()` (line 340) processes the queued request for Batch A\n   - Request serialization calls `batch.records()` (ProducerBatch line 481)\n   - `recordsBuilder.build()` returns MemoryRecords wrapping the original buffer\n   - **MemoryRecords does NOT copy data; it merely wraps the ByteBuffer reference**\n   - Serialization reads from the buffer, which now contains Batch B's data\n   - **Result**: Produce request header contains Batch B's topic/partition information instead of Batch A's\n\n### Why This Corrupts the Topic Name\n\nThe produce request format has two parts:\n1. **Header** (contains topic name, partition, etc.) — part of ProduceRequest structure\n2. **Records payload** — MemoryRecords wrapping the batch's ByteBuffer\n\nThe header is serialized from the batch's metadata AFTER the buffer has been deallocated and reused. When the buffer is reused, the topic name in the header becomes corrupted with data from the reused buffer.\n\n### Why CRC Validation Passes\n\nThe CRC checksum (ProduceResponse) covers only:\n- Key/value data\n- Headers\n- **NOT** the topic name (which is in the request header, not the record batch)\n\nTherefore, corrupted topic names bypass CRC validation.\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\nThe root cause is that `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` is called in `failBatch()` while the batch's request may still be queued in the network client.\n\n### Fix Strategy\n\n**Do NOT deallocate batches in the `failBatch()` path. Let them be deallocated through the normal response path in `handleProduceResponse()` or through explicit cleanup on disconnect.**\n\n### Code Changes\n\n**File**: `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java`\n\n#### Change 1: Remove premature deallocation in failBatch()\n\n```diff\n--- a/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java\n+++ b/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java\n@@ -828,13 +828,22 @@ public class Sender implements Runnable {\n      * we need to reset the producer id here.\n      */\n     private void failBatch(\n         ProducerBatch batch,\n         RuntimeException topLevelException,\n         Function<Integer, RuntimeException> recordExceptions,\n         boolean adjustSequenceNumbers\n     ) {\n         this.sensors.recordErrors(batch.topicPartition.topic(), batch.recordCount);\n\n         if (batch.completeExceptionally(topLevelException, recordExceptions)) {\n             if (transactionManager != null) {\n                 try {\n                     // This call can throw an exception in the rare case that there's an invalid state transition\n                     // attempted. Catch these so as not to interfere with the rest of the logic.\n                     transactionManager.handleFailedBatch(batch, topLevelException, adjustSequenceNumbers);\n                 } catch (Exception e) {\n                     log.debug(\\\"Encountered error when transaction manager was handling a failed batch\\\", e);\n                 }\n             }\n-            maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);\n+            // Note: We do NOT deallocate the batch here, even though its final state is now set to FAILED.\n+            // The batch may still have an active request queued in the network client's send buffer.\n+            // Deallocating the buffer here would cause the buffer to be returned to the pool and potentially\n+            // reused by another batch while the network client is still serializing this batch's request.\n+            // This would corrupt the serialized request data (topic name, partition, etc).\n+            // Instead, we only remove the batch from inFlightBatches tracking. The buffer will be deallocated\n+            // when the response is eventually received (or the connection times out/disconnects) in handleProduceResponse().\n+            maybeRemoveFromInflightBatches(batch);\n         }\n     }\n```\n\n#### Change 2: Handle deallocation of failed batches that complete through handleProduceResponse()\n\nThe existing code in `handleProduceResponse()` already handles deallocation properly:\n- Line 750 in `completeBatch()`: `if (batch.complete(...)) { maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch); }`\n\nThis code attempts to set the batch's final state to SUCCEEDED. If the batch was already marked FAILED, this will fail gracefully (ProducerBatch.done line 277-286 handles the FAILED -> SUCCEEDED transition by logging and ignoring). The batch will remain in `inFlightBatches` until:\n\n1. A response from broker arrives and is processed in `handleProduceResponse()`\n2. Network disconnect is detected (handled in same method at line 577-582)\n3. Request timeout occurs (handled at line 571-576)\n\nIn all these cases, `completeBatch()` is called which will deallocate the batch at line 750 via `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()`.\n\n#### Change 3: Add defensive guard for batches already deallocated\n\nTo handle any edge cases where a batch might be processed twice, add safety check in `deallocate()`:\n\n```diff\n--- a/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/RecordAccumulator.java\n+++ b/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/RecordAccumulator.java\n@@ -1027,8 +1027,14 @@ public class RecordAccumulator {\n      */\n     public void deallocate(ProducerBatch batch) {\n         incomplete.remove(batch);\n         // Only deallocate the batch if it is not a split batch because split batch are allocated outside the\n         // buffer pool.\n         if (!batch.isSplitBatch())\n-            free.deallocate(batch.buffer(), batch.initialCapacity());\n+            // Only deallocate if the batch still has its buffer. In rare cases, the batch might be\n+            // processed multiple times (e.g., marked failed via timeout, then receives response from broker).\n+            // Once deallocated, the buffer reference becomes invalid.\n+            if (batch.buffer() != null) {\n+                free.deallocate(batch.buffer(), batch.initialCapacity());\n+            }\n     }\n```\n\n## Analysis: Execution Flow Demonstrating the Bug\n\n### Normal (non-buggy) case:\n1. Batch drained at T1, request queued at T2, serialized at T3, response received at T4, deallocated at T4\n2. Buffer stays allocated while network client owns the request\n\n### Buggy case (what we fixed):\n1. Batch drained at T1\n2. Request queued at T2\n3. **Batch expires and marked FAILED at T2.5**\n4. **Buffer deallocated and returned to pool at T2.7**\n5. **New batch B allocated and reuses buffer at T2.8**\n6. Network client serializes request for batch A at T3\n7. **Corruption: Request has batch B's data in the buffer**\n8. Corrupted request sent to broker at T4\n9. Messages appear on wrong topic\n\n### Fixed case:\n1. Batch drained at T1\n2. Request queued at T2\n3. Batch expires and marked FAILED at T2.5\n4. **Buffer NOT deallocated** (fix prevents this)\n5. Network client serializes request for batch A at T3\n6. **Request has correct data from batch A's buffer**\n7. Response received at T4\n8. Batch deallocated at T4 (in handleProduceResponse)\n9. Buffer can now be reused safely\n\n## Summary\n\nThe race condition occurs because `failBatch()` deallocates a batch's buffer before the network client finishes serializing its request. By moving the deallocation to the `handleProduceResponse()` path (which is guaranteed to execute after serialization), we ensure the buffer remains valid throughout the entire request lifecycle.\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}

Line 395: Batches drained from accumulator\n    16→   - Line 396: Batches added to `inFlightBatches` tracking map\n    17→   - Line 406-408: Expired batches detected from `inFlightBatches`\n    18→   - Line 418: `failBatch()` called on expired batches\n    19→   - Line 442: `sendProduceRequests()` sends non-expired batches to network client\n    20→4. **Buffer deallocation path**:\n    21→   - Line 835: `failBatch()` calls `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` (line 173)\n    22→   - Line 173: Calls `accumulator.deallocate(batch)`\n    23→   - RecordAccumulator line 1032: Buffer returned to pool via `free.deallocate(batch.buffer())`\n    24→5. **Network client serialization**:\n    25→   - Line 914: `client.send(clientRequest)` queues request for serialization\n    26→   - Serialization happens later during `client.poll()` (line 340)\n    27→   - Serialization reads from `batch.records()` buffer (line 874)\n    28→\n    29→## Root Cause\n    30→\n    31→- **File**: `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java`\n    32→- **Function**: `failBatch()` (line 817-837) and call chain from `sendProducerData()` (line 357)\n    33→- **Line**: ~418 (expiration handling) and ~835 (deallocation)\n    34→- **Exact issue**: Line 835 calls `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch)` unconditionally after marking batch as failed\n    35→\n    36→## Explanation of the Race Condition\n    37→\n    38→### The Bug\n    39→\n    40→When a `ProducerBatch` expires while its network request is still queued in the network client's send buffer, the following race occurs:\n    41→\n    42→1. **Iteration N of `sendProducerData()`**:\n    43→   - Line 395: Batch A is drained and added to local `batches` map\n    44→   - Line 396: Batch A is added to `inFlightBatches` (tracking map)\n    45→   - Line 914: `client.send()` queues Batch A's produce request for later serialization\n    46→\n    47→2. **Before network client serialization** (within same or next iteration):\n    48→   - Line 406-408: Batch A is found in `expiredInflightBatches` (delivery timeout reached)\n    49→   - Line 418: `failBatch(Batch A)` is called\n    50→   - Line 825: `batch.completeExceptionally()` returns true (first time setting final state to FAILED)\n    51→   - Line 835: `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(Batch A)` is called\n    52→   - Line 173: `accumulator.deallocate(Batch A)` is called\n    53→   - RecordAccumulator line 1032: Batch A's ByteBuffer is returned to the `BufferPool`\n    54→\n    55→3. **BufferPool reuse** (concurrent with network serialization):\n    56→   - BufferPool allocates Batch A's buffer to Batch B (new batch)\n    57→   - Batch B writes records to the buffer\n    58→\n    59→4. **Network client serialization**:\n    60→   - `client.poll()` (line 340) processes the queued request for Batch A\n    61→   - Request serialization calls `batch.records()` (ProducerBatch line 481)\n    62→   - `recordsBuilder.build()` returns MemoryRecords wrapping the original buffer\n    63→   - **MemoryRecords does NOT copy data; it merely wraps the ByteBuffer reference**\n    64→   - Serialization reads from the buffer, which now contains Batch B's data\n    65→   - **Result**: Produce request header contains Batch B's topic/partition information instead of Batch A's\n    66→\n    67→### Why This Corrupts the Topic Name\n    68→\n    69→The produce request format has two parts:\n    70→1. **Header** (contains topic name, partition, etc.) — part of ProduceRequest structure\n    71→2. **Records payload** — MemoryRecords wrapping the batch's ByteBuffer\n    72→\n    73→The header is serialized from the batch's metadata AFTER the buffer has been deallocated and reused. When the buffer is reused, the topic name in the header becomes corrupted with data from the reused buffer.\n    74→\n    75→### Why CRC Validation Passes\n    76→\n    77→The CRC checksum (ProduceResponse) covers only:\n    78→- Key/value data\n    79→- Headers\n    80→- **NOT** the topic name (which is in the request header, not the record batch)\n    81→\n    82→Therefore, corrupted topic names bypass CRC validation.\n    83→\n    84→## Proposed Fix\n    85→\n    86→The root cause is that `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` is called in `failBatch()` while the batch's request may still be queued in the network client.\n    87→\n    88→### Fix Strategy\n    89→\n    90→**Do NOT deallocate batches in the `failBatch()` path. Let them be deallocated through the normal response path in `handleProduceResponse()` or through explicit cleanup on disconnect.**\n    91→\n    92→### Code Changes\n    93→\n    94→**File**: `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java`\n    95→\n    96→#### Change 1: Remove premature deallocation in failBatch()\n    97→\n    98→```diff\n    99→--- a/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java\n   100→+++ b/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java\n   101→@@ -828,13 +828,22 @@ public class Sender implements Runnable {\n   102→      * we need to reset the producer id here.\n   103→      */\n   104→     private void failBatch(\n   105→         ProducerBatch batch,\n   106→         RuntimeException topLevelException,\n   107→         Function<Integer, RuntimeException> recordExceptions,\n   108→         boolean adjustSequenceNumbers\n   109→     ) {\n   110→         this.sensors.recordErrors(batch.topicPartition.topic(), batch.recordCount);\n   111→\n   112→         if (batch.completeExceptionally(topLevelException, recordExceptions)) {\n   113→             if (transactionManager != null) {\n   114→                 try {\n   115→                     // This call can throw an exception in the rare case that there's an invalid state transition\n   116→                     // attempted. Catch these so as not to interfere with the rest of the logic.\n   117→                     transactionManager.handleFailedBatch(batch, topLevelException, adjustSequenceNumbers);\n   118→                 } catch (Exception e) {\n   119→                     log.debug(\\\"Encountered error when transaction manager was handling a failed batch\\\", e);\n   120→                 }\n   121→             }\n   122→-            maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);\n   123→+            // Note: We do NOT deallocate the batch here, even though its final state is now set to FAILED.\n   124→+            // The batch may still have an active request queued in the network client's send buffer.\n   125→+            // Deallocating the buffer here would cause the buffer to be returned to the pool and potentially\n   126→+            // reused by another batch while the network client is still serializing this batch's request.\n   127→+            // This would corrupt the serialized request data (topic name, partition, etc).\n   128→+            // Instead, we only remove the batch from inFlightBatches tracking. The buffer will be deallocated\n   129→+            // when the response is eventually received (or the connection times out/disconnects) in handleProduceResponse().\n   130→+            maybeRemoveFromInflightBatches(batch);\n   131→         }\n   132→     }\n   133→```\n   134→\n   135→#### Change 2: Handle deallocation of failed batches that complete through handleProduceResponse()\n   136→\n   137→The existing code in `handleProduceResponse()` already handles deallocation properly:\n   138→- Line 750 in `completeBatch()`: `if (batch.complete(...)) { maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch); }`\n   139→\n   140→This code attempts to set the batch's final state to SUCCEEDED. If the batch was already marked FAILED, this will fail gracefully (ProducerBatch.done line 277-286 handles the FAILED -> SUCCEEDED transition by logging and ignoring). The batch will remain in `inFlightBatches` until:\n   141→\n   142→1. A response from broker arrives and is processed in `handleProduceResponse()`\n   143→2. Network disconnect is detected (handled in same method at line 577-582)\n   144→3. Request timeout occurs (handled at line 571-576)\n   145→\n   146→In all these cases, `completeBatch()` is called which will deallocate the batch at line 750 via `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()`.\n   147→\n   148→#### Change 3: Add defensive guard for batches already deallocated\n   149→\n   150→To handle any edge cases where a batch might be processed twice, add safety check in `deallocate()`:\n   151→\n   152→```diff\n   153→--- a/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/RecordAccumulator.java\n   154→+++ b/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/RecordAccumulator.java\n   155→@@ -1027,8 +1027,14 @@ public class RecordAccumulator {\n   156→      */\n   157→     public void deallocate(ProducerBatch batch) {\n   158→         incomplete.remove(batch);\n   159→         // Only deallocate the batch if it is not a split batch because split batch are allocated outside the\n   160→         // buffer pool.\n   161→         if (!batch.isSplitBatch())\n   162→-            free.deallocate(batch.buffer(), batch.initialCapacity());\n   163→+            // Only deallocate if the batch still has its buffer. In rare cases, the batch might be\n   164→+            // processed multiple times (e.g., marked failed via timeout, then receives response from broker).\n   165→+            // Once deallocated, the buffer reference becomes invalid.\n   166→+            if (batch.buffer() != null) {\n   167→+                free.deallocate(batch.buffer(), batch.initialCapacity());\n   168→+            }\n   169→     }\n   170→```\n   171→\n   172→## Analysis: Execution Flow Demonstrating the Bug\n   173→\n   174→### Normal (non-buggy) case:\n   175→1. Batch drained at T1, request queued at T2, serialized at T3, response received at T4, deallocated at T4\n   176→2. Buffer stays allocated while network client owns the request\n   177→\n   178→### Buggy case (what we fixed):\n   179→1. Batch drained at T1\n   180→2. Request queued at T2\n   181→3. **Batch expires and marked FAILED at T2.5**\n   182→4. **Buffer deallocated and returned to pool at T2.7**\n   183→5. **New batch B allocated and reuses buffer at T2.8**\n   184→6. Network client serializes request for batch A at T3\n   185→7. **Corruption: Request has batch B's data in the buffer**\n   186→8. Corrupted request sent to broker at T4\n   187→9. Messages appear on wrong topic\n   188→\n   189→### Fixed case:\n   190→1. Batch drained at T1\n   191→2. Request queued at T2\n   192→3. Batch expires and marked FAILED at T2.5\n   193→4. **Buffer NOT deallocated** (fix prevents this)\n   194→5. Network client serializes request for batch A at T3\n   195→6. **Request has correct data from batch A's buffer**\n   196→7. Response received at T4\n   197→8. Batch deallocated at T4 (in handleProduceResponse)\n   198→9. Buffer can now be reused safely\n   199→\n   200→## Summary\n   201→\n   202→The race condition occurs because `failBatch()` deallocates a batch's buffer before the network client finishes serializing its request. By moving the deallocation to the `handleProduceResponse()` path (which is guaranteed to execute after serialization), we ensure the buffer remains valid throughout the entire request lifecycle.\n   203→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. Request serialization calls `batch.records()` (ProducerBatch line 481)\n   - `recordsBuilder.build()` returns MemoryRecords wrapping the original buffer\n   - **MemoryRecords does NOT copy data; it merely wraps the ByteBuffer reference**\n   - Serialization reads from the buffer, which now contains Batch B's data\n   - **Result**: Produce request header contains Batch B's topic/partition information instead of Batch A's\n\n### Why This Corrupts the Topic Name\n\nThe produce request format has two parts:\n1. **Header** (contains topic name, partition, etc.) — part of ProduceRequest structure\n2. **Records payload** — MemoryRecords wrapping the batch's ByteBuffer\n\nThe header is serialized from the batch's metadata AFTER the buffer has been deallocated and reused. When the buffer is reused, the topic name in the header becomes corrupted with data from the reused buffer.\n\n### Why CRC Validation Passes\n\nThe CRC checksum (ProduceResponse) covers only:\n- Key/value data\n- Headers\n- **NOT** the topic name (which is in the request header, not the record batch)\n\nTherefore, corrupted topic names bypass CRC validation.\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\nThe root cause is that `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` is called in `failBatch()` while the batch's request may still be queued in the network client.\n\n### Fix Strategy\n\n**Do NOT deallocate batches in the `failBatch()` path. Let them be deallocated through the normal response path in `handleProduceResponse()` or through explicit cleanup on disconnect.**\n\n### Code Changes\n\n**File**: `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java`\n\n#### Change 1: Remove premature deallocation in failBatch()\n\n```diff\n--- a/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java\n+++ b/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java\n@@ -828,13 +828,22 @@ public class Sender implements Runnable {\n      * we need to reset the producer id here.\n      */\n     private void failBatch(\n         ProducerBatch batch,\n         RuntimeException topLevelException,\n         Function<Integer, RuntimeException> recordExceptions,\n         boolean adjustSequenceNumbers\n     ) {\n         this.sensors.recordErrors(batch.topicPartition.topic(), batch.recordCount);\n\n         if (batch.completeExceptionally(topLevelException, recordExceptions)) {\n             if (transactionManager != null) {\n                 try {\n                     // This call can throw an exception in the rare case that there's an invalid state transition\n                     // attempted. Catch these so as not to interfere with the rest of the logic.\n                     transactionManager.handleFailedBatch(batch, topLevelException, adjustSequenceNumbers);\n                 } catch (Exception e) {\n                     log.debug(\\\"Encountered error when transaction manager was handling a failed batch\\\", e);\n                 }\n             }\n-            maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);\n+            // Note: We do NOT deallocate the batch here, even though its final state is now set to FAILED.\n+            // The batch may still have an active request queued in the network client's send buffer.\n+            // Deallocating the buffer here would cause the buffer to be returned to the pool and potentially\n+            // reused by another batch while the network client is still serializing this batch's request.\n+            // This would corrupt the serialized request data (topic name, partition, etc).\n+            // Instead, we only remove the batch from inFlightBatches tracking. The buffer will be deallocated\n+            // when the response is eventually received (or the connection times out/disconnects) in handleProduceResponse().\n+            maybeRemoveFromInflightBatches(batch);\n         }\n     }\n```\n\n#### Change 2: Handle deallocation of failed batches that complete through handleProduceResponse()\n\nThe existing code in `handleProduceResponse()` already handles deallocation properly:\n- Line 750 in `completeBatch()`: `if (batch.complete(...)) { maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch); }`\n\nThis code attempts to set the batch's final state to SUCCEEDED. If the batch was already marked FAILED, this will fail gracefully (ProducerBatch.done line 277-286 handles the FAILED -> SUCCEEDED transition by logging and ignoring). The batch will remain in `inFlightBatches` until:\n\n1. A response from broker arrives and is processed in `handleProduceResponse()`\n2. Network disconnect is detected (handled in same method at line 577-582)\n3. Request timeout occurs (handled at line 571-576)\n\nIn all these cases, `completeBatch()` is called which will deallocate the batch at line 750 via `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()`.\n\n#### Change 3: Add defensive guard for batches already deallocated\n\nTo handle any edge cases where a batch might be processed twice, add safety check in `deallocate()`:\n\n```diff\n--- a/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/RecordAccumulator.java\n+++ b/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/RecordAccumulator.java\n@@ -1027,8 +1027,14 @@ public class RecordAccumulator {\n      */\n     public void deallocate(ProducerBatch batch) {\n         incomplete.remove(batch);\n         // Only deallocate the batch if it is not a split batch because split batch are allocated outside the\n         // buffer pool.\n         if (!batch.isSplitBatch())\n-            free.deallocate(batch.buffer(), batch.initialCapacity());\n+            // Only deallocate if the batch still has its buffer. In rare cases, the batch might be\n+            // processed multiple times (e.g., marked failed via timeout, then receives response from broker).\n+            // Once deallocated, the buffer reference becomes invalid.\n+            if (batch.buffer() != null) {\n+                free.deallocate(batch.buffer(), batch.initialCapacity());\n+            }\n     }\n```\n\n## Analysis: Execution Flow Demonstrating the Bug\n\n### Normal (non-buggy) case:\n1. Batch drained at T1, request queued at T2, serialized at T3, response received at T4, deallocated at T4\n2. Buffer stays allocated while network client owns the request\n\n### Buggy case (what we fixed):\n1. Batch drained at T1\n2. Request queued at T2\n3. **Batch expires and marked FAILED at T2.5**\n4. **Buffer deallocated and returned to pool at T2.7**\n5. **New batch B allocated and reuses buffer at T2.8**\n6. Network client serializes request for batch A at T3\n7. **Corruption: Request has batch B's data in the buffer**\n8. Corrupted request sent to broker at T4\n9. Messages appear on wrong topic\n\n### Fixed case:\n1. Batch drained at T1\n2. Request queued at T2\n3. Batch expires and marked FAILED at T2.5\n4. **Buffer NOT deallocated** (fix prevents this)\n5. Network client serializes request for batch A at T3\n6. **Request has correct data from batch A's buffer**\n7. Response received at T4\n8. Batch deallocated at T4 (in handleProduceResponse)\n9. Buffer can now be reused safely\n\n## Summary\n\nThe race condition occurs because `failBatch()` deallocates a batch's buffer before the network client finishes serializing its request. By moving the deallocation to the `handleProduceResponse()` path (which is guaranteed to execute after serialization), we ensure the buffer remains valid throughout the entire request lifecycle.\n","numLines":203,"startLine":1,"totalLines":203}}}
